- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/jdk--742e735d$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# OpenJDK Security Provider Registration Framework

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in openjdk/jdk that implement the security provider registration framework. Identify: the base Provider class with putService() (java.security.Provider), the SunJCE provider that registers crypto algorithms, the SunJSSE provider for SSL/TLS factories, the SunEC provider for elliptic curve algorithms, the Sun provider for core algorithms, and the ProviderConfig lazy-loading mechanism that maps provider names to classes.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/jdk--742e735d.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` (openjdk/jdk)

Perfect! I have completed the comprehensive analysis of the Java security provider registration framework in openjdk/jdk. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've identified all the key Java source files implementing the OpenJDK security provider registration framework and created a detailed answer at `/workspace/answer.json`. The framework consists of:

### Core Components:

1. **Base Framework** - `Provider.java`: The abstract base class defining `putService()` method
2. **Core Providers**:
   - `SunJCE.java` - Cryptographic algorithms (RSA, DES, AES, HMAC, ChaCha20, etc.)
   - `SunJSSE.java` - SSL/TLS factories and contexts
   - `SunEC.java` - Elliptic curve cryptography
   - `Sun.java` - Core DSA, message digests, keystores, and PKIX

3. **Lazy-Loading Infrastructure**:
   - `ProviderConfig.java` - Maps provider names to classes with on-demand loading
   - `ProviderList.java` - Manages ordered provider lists
   - `Providers.java` - Central provider management with thread-local support

4. **Supporting Components**:
   - `SunEntries.java` - Service registry for Sun provider
   - `SunRsaSign.java` - RSA signature provider
   - `SunRsaSignEntries.java` - Service registry for RSA signing
   - `VerificationProvider.java` - JAR verification provider

The answer includes detailed symbols, the call chain, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how the framework works, the registration pattern used by all providers, and the lazy-loading mechanism that improves startup performance.

extends Properties and serves as the base for all security providers. It defines the `putService(Service s)` protected method used by all providers to register their cryptographic services.\\n\\n## Core Built-in Providers\\n\\n1. **SunJCE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java): Implements cryptographic algorithms including RSA encryption, DES, Triple DES, AES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC variants, ChaCha20, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Uses the `putService()` method to register all algorithms through helper methods in the constructor.\\n\\n2. **SunJSSE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): The Java Secure Socket Extension provider that registers SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext implementations for various TLS versions (TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore implementations.\\n\\n3. **SunEC Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ec/SunEC.java): Implements elliptic curve cryptography algorithms. Uses SunEntries to generate its service list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Infrastructure\\n\\n1. **ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): Encapsulates configuration for a single provider including the provider name and optional arguments. Implements lazy-loading logic through `doLoadProvider()` method which loads providers on-demand via reflection, using a maximum retry limit of 30 attempts to prevent infinite loops. Maps provider names (module or class names) to actual Provider instances.\\n\\n2. **ProviderList** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages an immutable ordered list of ProviderConfig entries. Supports operations like `fromSecurityProperties()` to load providers from java.security configuration, and `add()`/`insertAt()` for dynamic provider addition. Uses a dummy EMPTY_PROVIDER during initialization to avoid null checks.\\n\\n3. **Providers** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java): Central management class that maintains thread-local and system-wide provider lists. extends Properties and serves as the base for all security providers. Uses the `putService()` method to register all algorithms through helper methods in the constructor.\\n\\n2. **SunJSSE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): The Java Secure Socket Extension provider that registers SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext implementations for various TLS versions (TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore implementations.\\n\\n3. **SunEC Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ec/SunEC.java): Implements elliptic curve cryptography algorithms. Uses SunEntries to generate its service list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Infrastructure\\n\\n1. **ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): Encapsulates configuration for a single provider including the provider name and optional arguments. Implements lazy-loading logic through `doLoadProvider()` method which loads providers on-demand via reflection, using a maximum retry limit of 30 attempts to prevent infinite loops. Maps provider names (module or class names) to actual Provider instances.\\n\\n2. **ProviderList** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages an immutable ordered list of ProviderConfig entries. Supports operations like `fromSecurityProperties()` to load providers from java.security configuration, and `add()`/`insertAt()` for dynamic provider addition. Uses a dummy EMPTY_PROVIDER during initialization to avoid null checks.\\n\\n3. **Providers** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java): Central management class that maintains thread-local and system-wide provider lists. Initializes the default provider list from security properties at static initialization time. Contains the hardcoded list of providers used for JAR verification (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE) and provides `getSunProvider()` factory method.\\n\\n## Registration Pattern\\n\\nAll provider implementations follow a consistent pattern: (1) extend the Provider class, (2) call `super()` constructor with provider name and version, (3) register services using `putService(new Provider.Service(...))` where the Service inner class encapsulates the algorithm type, algorithm name, implementation class name, aliases, and attributes. This is demonstrated in SunJCE and SunJSSE through helper methods like `ps()`, and in Sun through SunEntries iterator pattern.\\n\\nThe lazy-loading mechanism via ProviderConfig enables providers to be loaded only when needed, improving startup performance while maintaining transparency to applications through the standard Security API.\"\n}\n",

extends Properties and serves as the base for all security providers. Uses the `putService()` method to register all algorithms through helper methods in the constructor.\\n\\n2. **SunJSSE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): The Java Secure Socket Extension provider that registers SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext implementations for various TLS versions (TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore implementations.\\n\\n3. **SunEC Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ec/SunEC.java): Implements elliptic curve cryptography algorithms. Contains an inner ProviderService class that overrides `newInstance()` to create signature, key pair generation, and algorithm parameter implementations for ECDSA variants and EdDSA.\\n\\n4. **Sun Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/provider/Sun.java): The core provider that implements DSA key generation, DSA signing, message digests (SHA-1, MD5), SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPathValidator and CertPathBuilder, and policy/configuration implementations. Uses SunEntries to generate its service list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Infrastructure\\n\\n1. **ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): Encapsulates configuration for a single provider including the provider name and optional arguments. Implements lazy-loading logic through `doLoadProvider()` method which loads providers on-demand via reflection, using a maximum retry limit of 30 attempts to prevent infinite loops. Maps provider names (module or class names) to actual Provider instances.\\n\\n2. **ProviderList** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages an immutable ordered list of ProviderConfig entries. Supports operations like `fromSecurityProperties()` to load providers from java.security configuration, and `add()`/`insertAt()` for dynamic provider addition. Uses a dummy EMPTY_PROVIDER during initialization to avoid null checks.\\n\\n3. **Providers** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java): Central management class that maintains thread-local and system-wide provider lists. Initializes the default provider list from security properties at static initialization time. Contains the hardcoded list of providers used for JAR verification (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE) and provides `getSunProvider()` factory method.\\n\\n## Registration Pattern\\n\\nAll provider implementations follow a consistent pattern: (1) extend the Provider class, (2) call `super()` constructor with provider name and version, (3) register services using `putService(new Provider.Service(...))` where the Service inner class encapsulates the algorithm type, algorithm name, implementation class name, aliases, and attributes. This is demonstrated in SunJCE and SunJSSE through helper methods like `ps()`, and in Sun through SunEntries iterator pattern.\\n\\nThe lazy-loading mechanism via ProviderConfig enables providers to be loaded only when needed, improving startup performance while maintaining transparency to applications through the standard Security API.\"\n}\n",
